  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1e9a8f7e-055b-4f00-86bf-aeff688f18c7'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14285633772392704648">The men on board HMS <i>Terror</i> have every expectation of triumph. As part of the 1845 Franklin Expedition, the first steam-powered vessels ever to search for the legendary Northwest Passage, they are as scientifically supported an enterprise as has ever set forth. As they enter a second summer in the Arctic Circle without a thaw, though, they are stranded in a nightmarish lan</span>
  <span id="freeText14285633772392704648" style="display:none">The men on board HMS <i>Terror</i> have every expectation of triumph. As part of the 1845 Franklin Expedition, the first steam-powered vessels ever to search for the legendary Northwest Passage, they are as scientifically supported an enterprise as has ever set forth. As they enter a second summer in the Arctic Circle without a thaw, though, they are stranded in a nightmarish landscape of encroaching ice and darkness. Endlessly cold, with diminishing rations, 126 men fight to survive with poisonous food, a dwindling supply of coal, and ships buckling in the grip of crushing ice. But their real enemy is far more terrifying. There is something out there in the frigid darkness: an unseen predator stalking their ship, a monstrous terror constantly clawing to get in.<br /><br />When the expedition's leader, Sir John Franklin, meets a terrible death, Captain Francis Crozier takes command and leads his surviving crewmen on a last, desperate attempt to flee south across the ice. With them travels an Inuit woman who cannot speak and who may be the key to survival, or the harbinger of their deaths. But as another winter approaches, as scurvy and starvation grow more terrible, and as the terror on the ice stalks them southward, Crozier and his men begin to fear that there is no escape.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14285633772392704648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/295134-what-do-you-think-dan-simmons-was-trying">What do you think Dan Simmons was trying to say with &quot;the terror&quot;? (The thing out on the ice, not the ship bound into the ice.)</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_295134'><a id="like_count_community_question_295134" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/295134?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">8 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F3974.The_Terror">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/295134-what-do-you-think-dan-simmons-was-trying">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/295134-what-do-you-think-dan-simmons-was-trying">See all 8 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/38148349-benjamin-atkinson"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1421976938i/38148349._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/38148349-benjamin-atkinson">Benjamin Atkinson</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I believe, IMHO, that Mr. Simmons was referring to the lack of humility that Western Society has displayed (see Titanic) and many other examples. The <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I believe, IMHO, that Mr. Simmons was referring to the lack of humility that Western Society has displayed (see Titanic) and many other examples. The terror in this novel is many things it is the physical, visceral hell those men lived through, it is the terror of the unknown. But ultimately, I believe, the overarching terror is that the men leading this incredible expedition brought everything with them except a true knowledge of how the indigenous peoples survived cold climates with minimal technology. Same problem seen in America's approach to Vietnam; we did not understand the situation on the ground before we attacked. Iraq, Afghanistan, ad infinitum. Thank you for your question. Do you have any great book recommendations for me. I love hard sci-fiction and anything to do with survival and the psychology of isolation<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Historically they were never found. Neither was Crozier or the Terror. Erebus was located a few years ago sunk and by way of sonar, Terror has not sho<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Historically they were never found. Neither was Crozier or the Terror. Erebus was located a few years ago sunk and by way of sonar, Terror has not shown up. Not many bodies were recovered. Many crew are still missing.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_225860751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225860751" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/225860751?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=horror-modern">horror-modern</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225860751" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15901948087396796636">To: Mr. Dan Simmons<br/>From: Associated Publishing Industries Unlimited, Ltd.<br/>Subject: Your Recent Submission <u>The Terror</u><br/><br/>Thank you for your recent submission. Unfortunately, at this time, we do not see a fit between your product and our company's goals. <br/><br/>Although our senior staff appreciated your technical ability, we noted several serious issues with your submission that need to be resolved prior to your product finding placement. These include, but are not limited to:<br/><br/>1. <i>Extensive and Excessive Length</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15901948087396796636" style="display:none">To: Mr. Dan Simmons<br />From: Associated Publishing Industries Unlimited, Ltd.<br />Subject: Your Recent Submission <u>The Terror</u><br /><br />Thank you for your recent submission. Unfortunately, at this time, we do not see a fit between your product and our company's goals. <br /><br />Although our senior staff appreciated your technical ability, we noted several serious issues with your submission that need to be resolved prior to your product finding placement. These include, but are not limited to:<br /><br />1. <i>Extensive and Excessive Length.</i> A common error made by both the reading public and the writing community is that the modern novel must exceed 700 plus pages. The success of the Harry Potter series has only contributed to this misunderstanding. What many fail to understand is that this is simply the result of spacing and font size; the truth of the matter is that novels like those written by Ms. Rowling are no larger than any given novel by Beatrix Potter. Despite the fixation on what are basically large-print serials, our focus groups more frequently maintain that "The Shorter, The Better" - particularly given their short attention spans and addiction to pop culture media e.g. Us Magazine, Jersey Shore, Charlie Sheen, and the like.<br /><br />2. <i>Lack of Genre.</i> Your product appears to include traits from the Historical Novel, the Horror Novel (specifically its subset, the Monster Novel), and the Metaphysical Odyssey. Associated Publishing Industries Unlimited, Ltd. products must strictly adhere to our "One Novel, One Genre" company philosophy. The general reading public is a busy public, and have no time for the perplexing muddiness of genre mixing-and-matching.<br /><br />3. (a) <i>Lack of Traditional Romance;</i> <br />(b) <i>Negative AND Positive Depictions of Homosexual Activity;</i><br />(c) <i>Interracial Sexuality Not Resulting in Punishment and/or Death of Non-White Character by Novel's End.</i> <br /><br />Please understand that our editorial staff has no personal issues with any of the above-noted items (in fact, our marketing department actively supports the targeting of the lucrative Gay/Homosexual demographic within our Ghettoized Associated Publishing Industries Unlimited, Ltd. subset label). However, the presence of <u>all three</u> alternative lifestyle choices/options within a single novel - one intended for mainstream consumption - can only yield confused, 'buy-shy' reactions from our reading public.<br /><br />4. (a) <i>Lack of Resolution.</i> Your novel does not have a solid ending. It only offers questions, not answers. Additionally, the "dreamlike tone" of the final pages were off-puttingly "poetic" "ambiguous" and "transcendent"... three adjectives that our focus groups vehemently reject when considering reading options. this Lack of Resolution would not necessarily be problematic if your submission was intended to be the first in a multi-novel saga; however it is quite clear from your ending that another issue is <br />(b) <i>Lack of Potential for Sequel or Series</i>.<br /><br />5. <i>Too Many Details</i>. oh, and 6. <i>Too Many Big Words</i>.<br /><br />We sincerely thank you for your time/effort.<br /><br />Signed,<br /><br />An Associated Publishing Industries Unlimited, Ltd. Representative</span>

<div id="review_92765192" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92765192" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92765192?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=tastes-like-people">tastes-like-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=it-is-for-class">it-is-for-class</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92765192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4852190805917715302">**lo! i have made a readalike list for this book over on riffle!** <br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.rifflebooks.com/list/254279?utm_campaign=rifflesocialshare&utm_medium=twitter&utm_source=riffleshare'>http://www.rifflebooks.com/list/25427...</a><br/><br/>oh my god, let me never get scurvy.<br/><br/>i am glad i am such a grad-school overachiever. for both the horror/sci-fi and mystery portions of my readers' advisory class, i have read one extra title from the selection list, and both times, i have liked the extra title best. (i did not choose to read an extra romance title, so we will never know how that would have turned out, alas)<br/><br/>this book is a rar</span>
  <span id="freeText4852190805917715302" style="display:none">**lo! i have made a readalike list for this book over on riffle!** <br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.rifflebooks.com/list/254279?utm_campaign=rifflesocialshare&amp;utm_medium=twitter&amp;utm_source=riffleshare">http://www.rifflebooks.com/list/25427...</a><br><br>oh my god, let me never get scurvy.<br><br>i am glad i am such a grad-school overachiever. for both the horror/sci-fi and mystery portions of my readers' advisory class, i have read one extra title from the selection list, and both times, i have liked the extra title best. (i did not choose to read an extra romance title, so we will never know how that would have turned out, alas)<br><br>this book is a rare combination of <i>to the lighthouse</i>, and <i>the thing</i>, with hardy-esque occurrences of misunderstanding and some cannibalism thrown in for the kiddies. plus boats and ice and monster.<br><br>like <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0435625/" rel="nofollow noopener">the descent</a>, it is the supernatural elements of the story that end up being the least scary. nature is scary enough. cave-exploration, even for feisty extreme-sport doing, athletic-looking girls, becomes terrifying, even before any monsters show up. monsters are icing. for this book, scurvy, madness, murder, temperatures of 78 degrees below zero, starvation, frostbite, gangrene, botulism, did i mention scurvy??- i mean, isn't that enough without a giant monster stalking and eating your seamen? <br><br>but i am,to my great dismay, not easily scared.this, to me, was the most promising trailer in the world: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2lm2hZ50sN4">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2lm2hZ...</a> but the movie was not scary, and in fact made me cross because of the ways in which it was not scary. i thought i had finally met my match, but i wound up being utterly disappointed. being scared is not too much to hope for, is it?? this book, while it is not going to keep me up tonight, has several really good "oh shit" moments. (and i hope that answers lori's question)<br><br>i love the cold, but this book made me pray for global warming to hurry up and save these poor men. (this feeling will last until one of you jokers sends me a picture of a sad polar bear - awwww) but seriously, shit is COLD!! <br><br>and i got so <i>into</i> the book that i took the wrong bus on monday and traveled a half hour in the wrong direction before looking up from the book to realize my mistake, and also skipped work (ostensibly because of residual bad-feeling from hellish customers yesterday and faulty alarm clock [both true:], but also because i wanted to finish this book before the ending could get ruined for me in class tonight)<br><br>it is an amazingly well-researched book, which may ruin it as horror genre-fiction for people who want their horror fast, cheap, and hard. there are tons of details about rigging and naval protocol and ice conditions and many repetitions of the survivor's names - there are echoes of <i>moby dick</i> here, in its dullish bits about whale anatomy that might be a staple of maritime fiction for all i know, but make the progress a little slower than the monstrous stephen king i read as the other horror title for this class. i think all the details add too much weight to the story to let it retain its status as genre fiction. for myself i would consider it historical fiction with some supernatural zazz. <br><br>but it remains totally absorbing, totally gripping, and despite all the questions i raised about the pacing, it is ultimately scarier than the king, whose characters remain cartoonish and too one-dimensional to be scary. except for large marge, cartoons are not scary. here, the danger seems imminent - there are incredible moments of tension and so many beloved characters having unfortunate things happen to them. do not become attached to any of them, because in the end, many seamen are swallowed, and several are spit out. <br><br>(that was unavoidable and you know it)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

<div id="review_70668807" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70668807" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411956191p2/1219253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70668807?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=blog">blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=crap">crap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=book-club-made-me-do-it">book-club-made-me-do-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70668807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14678487241539071808">September 7, 2010: I don't want to talk about it right now. It's too soon and the pain is still too fresh. I shall review on another day.<br/><br/>September 17, 2010: It's been well over a week since my encounter with <i>The Terror</i> and the thought of writing a review still exhausts me, but here it goes. <br/><br/>I have read many glowing reviews of <i>The Terror</i>. That is, in fact, why I bought it. I mean, check out this kick ass plot: <br/><br/>Two British ships, the Terror and the Erebus, are frozen in the polar sea for years, wa</span>
  <span id="freeText14678487241539071808" style="display:none">September 7, 2010: I don't want to talk about it right now. It's too soon and the pain is still too fresh. I shall review on another day.<br /><br />September 17, 2010: It's been well over a week since my encounter with <i>The Terror</i> and the thought of writing a review still exhausts me, but here it goes. <br /><br />I have read many glowing reviews of <i>The Terror</i>. That is, in fact, why I bought it. I mean, check out this kick ass plot: <br /><br />Two British ships, the Terror and the Erebus, are frozen in the polar sea for years, waiting in vain for a summer thaw. This is, of course, based upon the doomed Franklin expedition, so we have some serious history going on here. Now, add to that a dash of the supernatural--something is out there on the ice. It terrorizes the men, seeming to materialize from nowhere. It's three times the size of a polar bear and has the vicious, bloodthirsty nature of a predator, as well as the keen intelligence of a man. It's like a giant cat toying with the two ships as if they were terrified mice in a corner. There's nowhere to go, guns don't faze the the thing the men dub "The Terror", and, now, the food supply is running out.<br /><br />That's some frightening shit. It's the arctic. That alone is frightening. It can drive a man insane. It's the nothingness. The whiteness. The endless-ness. Howard Moon and Vince Noir <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9IjGNJPNyzU" rel="nofollow noopener">knew not to take the tundra lightly</a>.<br /><br />And that's part of what ruined the book in the beginning. All I could think as I read the first few chapters was "ice floe, nowhere to go." I think that might have taken away from the tone a bit.<br /><br />But here are some other more text-based reasons for the seething black pit of hatred that I have for this book:<br /><br />a) History or supernatural, Simmons needs to pick a side because the two storylines always seemed to run parallel to one another and never quite came together. It was like, "Okay, for 100 pages, I'm going to have the men fearing for their lives as this thing attacks them. I'm going to build tension and suspense and have my readers empathetically shitting down both legs! And then I'm going to flashback for 50 pages to boring nautical talk amongst stuffy British types before the expedition and then spend 150 pages talking about Welsh Wigs and Goldner food tins and building sledges and maybe I'll even talk about buggering, but no mention whatsoever of the monster for another 50 pages!" Simmons was at his best when describing the encounters between the men and the thing on the ice, but these moments were so few and far between that I just got to the point where I didn't care anymore. <br /><br />b) Too much historical minutiae. The book should have been 300 pages shorter. There were entire sections that didn't add anything to the narrative. I like my history like I like my men: short and concise. <br /><br />c) Scurvy is some wicked bad shite. A slow death by scurvy is undoubtedly one of the worst ways to die. But do you know what's worse? A slow death by reading endless accounts of the symptoms of scurvy.<br /><br />d) There are no likeable characters. In fact, there is little to differentiate one man from another. If you left out the dialogue tags, it would have sounded like one man having a conversation with himself. The only character I like is Pangle, who, alas, appears in just a chapter or two of this 766 page behemoth. <br /><br />e) I was really pissed when I finally found out what the thing was. The main reason? THAT'S what I wanted to read more about. And it took roughly 700 pages to get to a point where I was actually interested and intrigued and it cut me off. <br /><br />There were some bright spots. When Simmons wrote about the thing attacking the men, leaving bait for them and taunting them, he evoked moments that were truly terrifying and suspenseful. However, there just weren't enough of them. Sure, the attempts to survive against cold, hunger, and disease should have been compelling stuff, but they made for anemic reading when pitted against a terrifying adversary without name or shape. Also, the chapter in which the men throw a carnivale and erect tents that mirror the rooms in Edgar Allan Poe's <i>The Masque of the Red Death</i> is admittedly brilliant. <br /><br />When it comes right down to it, though, The Mighty Boosh did a far superior job of capturing the terror of the arctic. When Howard admonishes Vince that "The arctic is no respecter of fashion," I still get chills. The same cannot be said of my reaction to <i>The Terror</i>. <br /><br />Cross posted at <a href="http://viiamanda.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Insignificant Cinder</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14678487241539071808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1686175019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1686175019" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1686175019?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780316008075" href="/book/show/3708616-the-terror">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=horror-etc">horror-etc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1686175019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4031389889098264215"><b>UPDATE:</b> $2.99 on kindle US 7-27-17<br/><br/><b>People, just turn around and go home!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467938765ra/19648238.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I probably shouldn't have went and read some facts about the history of this book because I might mess this review up. It's just so freaking interesting and I want to read about it. The author left a lot of resources for books at the end and there is one I'm going to try to get for sure. <br/><br/>The fact that Dan Simmons added an horror element to a historic novel is pretty awesome. And there are so many characters that I liked in th</span>
  <span id="freeText4031389889098264215" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE:</b> $2.99 on kindle US 7-27-17<br><br><b>People, just turn around and go home!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467938765ra/19648238.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I probably shouldn't have went and read some facts about the history of this book because I might mess this review up. It's just so freaking interesting and I want to read about it. The author left a lot of resources for books at the end and there is one I'm going to try to get for sure. <br><br>The fact that Dan Simmons added an horror element to a historic novel is pretty awesome. And there are so many characters that I liked in the book and well. . . you know what happens if you read anything about the real story. <br><br>Some parts of the book had me confused because it would go back and forth at different times but I pretty much know what's going on. Captain Sir John Franklin and Captain Crozier take the HMS Terror and HMS Erebus out to try to go through the Northwest Passage, which was called the 1845 Franklin Expedition. And it's doomed!!!! Not only do they get stuck out there for a couple of years, they have some monster thing &lt;---(I know what the monster thing is) killing them, along with scurvy, starvation, random stuff, etc. <br><br>I LOVE the cold weather and WINTER is my favorite, but not this kind of stuff. Not being stuck in the ice in the middle of no where land with minus a million degrees with food running out, disease running all around, oh and lets not forget the monster! <br><br>I liked Dr. Harry D. S. Goodsir, he is one of the surgeons on the ships and after awhile he has an epiphany: <br><br><b>•One reason that Dr. Harry D. S. Goodsir had insisted on coming along on this exploration party was to prove that he was as strong and able a man as most of his crewmates. He soon realized that he wasn't.•</b><br><br>He's a very good man and does all he can for the crew members. He also keeps a diary which I enjoyed reading because it gave his point of view on things. <br><br>There is an Esquimaux lady that is on the Terror. They call her Silence because something chewed off her tongue. Yeah! She was brought there with her father or husband, they are not sure and I will let you read about that little mystery. I was freaked out by Silence the whole book. But there was a lot more going on there than meets the eye. <br><br>One of my favorite crew members was Irving, he was such a nice guy and he was told by Captain Crozier to watch over Silence because he didn't trust her. Boy did he see some crazy stuff going on with her. <br><br>I also liked Captain Crozier, Fitzjams who took over for Sir John, Mr. Diggle and Blanky. I loathed a man named Hickey. He was more evil than the monster I do believe and I wish he would have had some great torture befall him! Trust me, you won't like him either! <br><br>The story isn't just about the monster, this is a big tome of a book at almost 1000 pages but the monster isn't in it a whole lot. The story is about other horrible things that happen. The worries of what the crew is going to do when they are running out of food and find out that food is tainted (true story about the tainted food), running low on coal, people catching scurvy and dying a slow horrendous death, the cold, don't forget the cold. Some really nasty stuff happens that had to do with the cold. <br><br>But that monster does some crazy stuff. It's almost like he has a sick sense of humor! <br><br><b>•"It?" snaps Crozier. "One body? Back on the ship?" This makes no sense at all to the Terror's captain. "I thought you said both Strong and Evans were back."<br>Third Lieutenant Irving's entire face is frostbite white now. "They are, Captain. Or at least half of them. When we went to look at the body propped up there at the stern, it fell over and . . . well . . . came apart. As best we can tell, it's Billy Strong from the waist up. Tommy Evans from the waist down."<br>Crozier and Fitzjames can only look at each other.•</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453427379ra/17826011.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You never know what you will find in the never ending night! <br><br><b>•On a Tuesday dogwatch in the third week of November, the thing from the ice came aboard the Erebus and took the well-liked bosun, Mr. Thomas Terry, snatching him from his post near the stern, leaving only the man's head on the railing.•</b><br><br>I thought this was a really good book. I did think it was a bit long as a few parts dragged for me. And that's not because it's a tome, I have a few favorite tomes that are bigger than this one. Either way, I still very much enjoyed it and the ending and finding things out was so cool. Of course at one part you start to get an idea of what it's going to be about. And it took a turn I didn't see coming! <br><br>I will leave you with a picture of the Erebus they found in 2014/2015, I forget what the article said now but you can google it. They still haven't found Terror. They also found mummified corpses and stuff so be prepared when you google! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468793580i/19746588._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/07/the-terror-by-dan-simmons.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4031389889098264215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2210591801" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2210591801" />
    <a title="Ginger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger"><img alt="Ginger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593449448p2/14097149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2210591801?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginger" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger">Ginger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6279969-the-terror">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2210591801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1057431932813314775"><b>Whew! I finished it. Wowza!</b><br/>This is such a long book!!!!!!!<br/><br/>Don’t go into this one unless you enjoy big books, having the patience to let the story evolve and knowing that the pace can be slow at times.<br/><br/>I stuck in there from the beginning and the ending was well worth it! I was struggling in the beginning because the first 10 or so chapters in this book alternate between the present and the past when the Franklin expedition was started.<br/>It also has different POV chapters with characters so also know</span>
  <span id="freeText1057431932813314775" style="display:none"><b>Whew! I finished it. Wowza!</b><br>This is such a long book!!!!!!!<br><br>Don’t go into this one unless you enjoy big books, having the patience to let the story evolve and knowing that the pace can be slow at times.<br><br>I stuck in there from the beginning and the ending was well worth it! I was struggling in the beginning because the first 10 or so chapters in this book alternate between the present and the past when the Franklin expedition was started.<br>It also has different POV chapters with characters so also know that going in as well. You'll figure out who everyone is if you just take the time to let the story develop.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520353828i/25171414._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While reading <b>
  <i>The Terror</i>
</b> during winter, I always felt cold. This story sucks all the warmth from you from the below freezing temperatures in the book, the bleak surroundings and the isolation that the Franklin expedition endured. The Arctic was its own character in this book with the constant darkness and freezing conditions.<br>Good grief, I now need to go on a vacation to a warm, tropical island after reading this book!<br><br>This was a re-telling of the Franklin expedition from the details of the officers, seamen and the steps they took that got them stuck in the ice during the period of 1845-1848 near King William Island. The Royal Navy wanted to find a Northwest Passage from Britain to China and going through the Arctic was the steps they wanted to take to accomplish this.<br>In the Royal Navy’s mind, whether this expedition made it was another story.<br>Just keeping trying until they can get that Chinese tea and opium! It's gold I tell ya!<br><br><i>Dan Simmons</i> not only used the real names of the crew from <i>HMS Erebus</i> and <i>HMS Terror</i> but he used historical details of the nautical life during that time and geographical locations to really give this book staying power. I kept thinking, is this non-fiction but then the white, monster-like Yeti would come into the next chapter and I would say, “Nope!”.<br><br>The best part of this book was finding out that men can be more of a monster then the "demonthing" monster. <i>Simmons</i> writes this well and I experienced such hatred and despair while reading the last 25% of this book!<br>Jesus, I wanted to turn into the white, monster-like Yeti myself and kill some people!<br><br>I’m still not sure how to categorize this book. I’m guessing its a main dish of historical fiction, a side dish of some horror with a dessert of magical realism.<br>I really enjoyed the ending. It ended on a high note and I was satisfied with slogging through the Arctic and the slow beginning to get there!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1057431932813314775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1098490251" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1098490251" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1098490251?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1098490251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer226909726225722577">This is so good!!!!!!!! What took me so long to read this?????<br/><br/>The men aboard the HHS Terror believe they will be the ones to successfully search for the Northwest Passage. The year is 1845 and the Franklin Expedition is steam-powered and after spending another a second summer in the arctic circle, their rations begin to dwindle, men's spirits begin to plummet and there is no end to the ice, cold and darkness. As the men begin to show signs of scurvy, they also are confronted by poisonous food, c</span>
  <span id="freeText226909726225722577" style="display:none">This is so good!!!!!!!! What took me so long to read this?????<br /><br />The men aboard the HHS Terror believe they will be the ones to successfully search for the Northwest Passage. The year is 1845 and the Franklin Expedition is steam-powered and after spending another a second summer in the arctic circle, their rations begin to dwindle, men's spirits begin to plummet and there is no end to the ice, cold and darkness. As the men begin to show signs of scurvy, they also are confronted by poisonous food, crushing ice, and an unseen "terror" on the ice which seems to be plucking them off one by one.<br /><br />Plus, there is the Inuit/Esquimaux woman who cannot speak but who has survival skills that leave the men in awe and frightened at the same time. She seems to be able to hunt and thrive in a harsh environment. Is she a witch? Can she be trusted? and how is she able to slip away without notice?<br /><br />When Sir John Franklin meets a gruesome death, Captain Francais Crozier takes charge and leads the men on a last-ditch effort to take their chances and flee on the ice. Will they survive? Will they starve to death? Will scurvy be their downfall or will the real "terror" on the ice be the death of them all?<br /><br />This is a monster of a book. It's HUGE and cannot be read fast. It is to be savored and read slowly. There are many characters with stories to tell. The first 5--70 pages were a little slow for me but as the story builds, I found my heart racing in fear for the characters (especially when Blanky was desperately trying to get away by climbing higher and higher through the ropes to survive).<br /><br />Whew!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="226909726225722577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_398148863" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/398148863" />
    <a title="Michael Fierce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6880123-michael-fierce"><img alt="Michael Fierce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602282713p2/6880123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/398148863?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Fierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Fierce" href="/user/show/6880123-michael-fierce">Michael Fierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780316008075" href="/book/show/3708616-the-terror">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of historical fiction and oldschool books by Poe, Kipling, Algernon Blackwood &amp; Ambrose Bierce</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=creature">creature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer398148863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3349511414365058423"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749325._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3708616.The_Terror' title='The Terror by Dan Simmons' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Terror</a> is a fictional tale based on the real life experience of the notoriously doomed <b>John Franklin Expedition</b>.<br/><br/>These brave men journeyed hundreds of miles by sea voyage in the <b>HMS Erebus</b> and <b>HMS Terror</b>, part of the British Naval fleet sent to the Arctic to force the Northwest Passage in <b>1845–1848</b>, and then travelled the rest on foot into the desolate, below-freezing temperatures of the Arctic wasteland.<br/><br/><pre>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749326.png' width='300' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</pre><b>All died or were never seen or heard from ever again</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749327.jpg' width='400' height='283' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons' title='Dan Simmons' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dan Simmons</a> imaginative story ex</span>
  <span id="freeText3349511414365058423" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749325._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3708616.The_Terror" title="The Terror by Dan Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">The Terror</a> is a fictional tale based on the real life experience of the notoriously doomed <b>John Franklin Expedition</b>.<br><br>These brave men journeyed hundreds of miles by sea voyage in the <b>HMS Erebus</b> and <b>HMS Terror</b>, part of the British Naval fleet sent to the Arctic to force the Northwest Passage in <b>1845–1848</b>, and then travelled the rest on foot into the desolate, below-freezing temperatures of the Arctic wasteland.<br><br><pre>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749326.png" width="300" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</pre><b>All died or were never seen or heard from ever again</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749327.jpg" width="400" height="283" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons" title="Dan Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">Dan Simmons</a> imaginative story explains how and why. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3708616.The_Terror" title="The Terror by Dan Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">The Terror</a> is a book drawn from a historical background so deep and so thoroughly well-researched that I'm quite sure I've never heard of any other writer of fiction attempting to do so at this level ever before. <br><br>For those that like to pick apart every bit of a story with a goal in mind to repute the validity of the facts given, you won't find much to work with here. <br><br>Set in the harshest conditions, with handfuls of men that may be hard to discern not only which side of the fence they're on, but just who is who for a ways, these characters aren't so much as enjoyable as they are absorbing. As their living conditions become more severe and their hardships grow more intense, good decision-making is made less and less often. Way below freezing temperatures, sparse food supplies, sickness, soreness, etc., would be tragic for even the most stalwart of men.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749328.jpg" width="400" height="205" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3708616.The_Terror" title="The Terror by Dan Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">The Terror</a>, providentially, is more than all this. What is it exactly? ~ This <i>is</i> a horror book, right? Yes. Even though it didn't have to be. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons" title="Dan Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">Dan Simmons</a> could have left out all the fantastical elements in his historical tale and it would've been enough to cringe to and have nightmares about and be fascinated by all the same. But, he didn't stop there, thankfully. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454651379i/17995018._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="205" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So what is <b>The Terror</b> exactly? Is it a man? Is it natural, man-made, myth or legend? The word <b>Tuunbaq</b> comes up. Is it a living creature, a guardian spirit, or an evil elder monster from eons past, or maybe something from another world?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749329._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="582" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><pre>
  <b> ~ Is it the Wendigo? Or possibly a Yeti? ~</b>
  <br>
</pre><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749330.jpg" width="400" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><pre>
  <b> ~ A Polar Bear gone mad with frenzy? ~</b>
</pre> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749331._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><pre>
  <b> ~ Is it the mythical Tuunbaq, maybe? ~ </b>
</pre><br>I can't say. <br><br>The story itself is very long, a bit heavy, hopeless, and as can only be expected, if you don't stay on it you will probably confuse a few of the officers with eachother which could result in you wanting to forget the whole thing altogether. <br><br>This book cannot be compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons" title="Dan Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">Simmons</a> previous novels in any shape or form. This book is not science-fiction nor does it have the framework or set-up of a traditional horror tale either. <br><br>For anyone fascinated with historical adventures and cryptid horror and for readers who crave oldschool antiquated storytelling. <br><br>It takes an investment of time and patience beyond the norm that should be very rewarding if you stay with it until the end. I thought it was truly great and really enjoyed all the finer details that breached to the surface.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749332._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you are a modern reader and you only like *page-turners*, this is certainly not for you. If you have a million and one things going on at once, just say no for now. If you are into comic book type action of super-heroic proportions, not for you. If you like quick answers and are impatient in any way I suggest reading something else. If you are somebody who needs happy American-style endings to your movie, where you finally get the girl and there's a big smooch in the end with sunlight or fireworks streaming in the background, don't even touch this book for fear you might be infected by the dreadful truth of reality. <br><br>There are many reasons why you should want to read this though. In this book you will share and feel the experience the crew are feeling: the cold, the despair, the loneliness, the dread and terror of the unknown, unstoppable creature, and the tragic understanding of, what inevitably feels to be, a hopeless outcome. You might feel the need to put on layers and layers of clothing, and stand so close to a fire you may be tempted to put your hands and feet right into it. You will feel like you are living this book. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380388662i/749333.jpg" width="250" height="192" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I believe it is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons" title="Dan Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">Dan Simmons</a> magnum opus. I give it 5 stars not because I'm necesarily going to return and re-read it again anytime soon but because, other than being a tad too long, it is flawless. It doesn't fall into modern traps or pitfalls of always trying to please the reader nor does it have the feeling of a Hollywood movie where you know your main characters are going to survive to the end, regardless of any other surprises. <br><br>This is the real deal. Live it. Experience it. Draw from it. <br><br>Then pick up some fluffy fun read you can rollercoaster through for 2 days straight to a walloping climax so you can recuperate and recover. <br><br><b>*</b> For fans of the book, you will be glad to know AMC is bringing it to television in the form of a tv series and if that news isn't good enough, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/31205.Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott" rel="nofollow noopener">Ridley Scott</a> is purportedly producing it and my guess is he may even direct an episode or two.<br><br><b>**</b> There have been several releases of this book, even a few just recently. I prefer the standard-sized 2009 paperback release. It has a little better cover art than some of the others, having distinct yellow and white embossed lettering, and inside and on the back, a lot of cool quotes and kudo's by reviewers and other notable authors. <br><br>Kind of fun to read what others have to say about this extraordinary novel. <br><br><b>Highly recommended!!!!! </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454651850i/17995037.png" width="78" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3349511414365058423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2149608496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2149608496" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65909643-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515603070p2/65909643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2149608496?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/65909643-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2149608496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5239004995055774686">Why am I reading so many books about the cold? Maybe because it's freezing here in Chicago!<br/><br/>This is a buddy read with Cristina, and I'll review as I go.<br/><br/>The first couple of hundred pages were surprisingly slow-going. There was very little propulsion about the plot--just occasional glimpses of the "terror" along with long passages of backstory that I didn't really find compelling. I don't know why I reacted like that. Maybe it was because I'd just read Crime and Punishment, another (and very differ</span>
  <span id="freeText5239004995055774686" style="display:none">Why am I reading so many books about the cold? Maybe because it's freezing here in Chicago!<br /><br />This is a buddy read with Cristina, and I'll review as I go.<br /><br />The first couple of hundred pages were surprisingly slow-going. There was very little propulsion about the plot--just occasional glimpses of the "terror" along with long passages of backstory that I didn't really find compelling. I don't know why I reacted like that. Maybe it was because I'd just read Crime and Punishment, another (and very different) tome that managed to be fascinating throughout. Or maybe it was the prose, which isn't terribly stylish. I'm always a sucker for great prose, and I miss it when it isn't there. At that point, I would have given the book two or maybe three stars.<br /><br />Then, at some point, things brightened up--the plot started shifting into gear, with all the various elements (the terror, the ice, scurvy, boredom, and inter-character conflict) starting to come together. I still think it took too long for that to happen, but boy, I'm glad it did!<br /><br />[Some spoilers follow]<br /><br />***<br /><br />I love the scene of the Carnival, no doubt because it self-consciously replicates Poe's The Masque of the Red Death. You just knew, given that setup, that the creature would strike, but it was quite well-done all the same. And the scene where Irving watches the creature and Lady Silence together was just magical. It deepened the sense of the creature as not merely being a source of terror, but also perhaps something more.<br /><br />Of course, against the backdrop of the creature striking, we have the "ticking clock" in the form of scurvy and running out of food. The sailors need to do something to escape, and their ice-bound ships will not suffice. What can they do? It's a terrific source of tension.<br /><br />***<br /><br />In the end they make an ill-fated attempt to cross the ice by foot, and here is where the interpersonal tensions come to a head. It's also where we see, in shocking terms, just what the cold does to a human body. The creature recedes somewhat into the background as the elements take over. I may have wished for more of a confrontation with the creature, as it seems to emerge at times conveniently, only to fade away when its presence is inconvenient, but this is a minor quibble. <br /><br />In the end, the group splinters, and a new source of evil in the form of Cornelius Hickey comes to the front of the stage. The pages here are quite gripping, even as the moral valence isn't terribly complicated.<br /><br />What does become complicated, and what ultimately elevates this book, is the relationship between Captain Crozier and "Lady Silence" that emerges after Crozier is left for dead by Hickey and his band. What's interesting is how Crozier changes and becomes like an Eskimo himself--how he becomes a different person. The climax is when the creature emerges and cuts out his tongue just as it had Lady Silence's, and while this is never really explained, I took it as a metaphor for the limits of language itself--how they had to free themselves from language to see beyond its obscuring haze of words. In the end, much of the final part of the book is interwoven with songs and language taken from the Eskimo, and while I couldn't understand it, it nonetheless had a certain power. Like a Latin Mass, the sounds themselves conveyed a certain meaning beyond the rational, which may have been part of the point--that all that British rationalism only got the men killed, while the liturgical melding of Crozier and Lady Silence and the landscape itself was what saved him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5239004995055774686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1236416426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1236416426" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1236416426?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1236416426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7057344272615893587"><i>See this review and more like it at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookbastion.net'>www.bookbastion.net</a>!</i><br/>_______<br/><br/>I'm late to the party with this read, I know, but The Terror just came onto my radar when I realized that AMC was turning it into a television show. <b>I'm a book-over-movie/tv adaptation purist.</b> So many details end up falling to the wayside in an adaptation - for example, I've watched one episode of the show, and already spotted a major difference from the book. I knew I'd want to experience this story as Dan Simmons originally told it</span>
  <span id="freeText7057344272615893587" style="display:none"><i>See this review and more like it at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookbastion.net">www.bookbastion.net</a>!</i><br>_______<br><br>I'm late to the party with this read, I know, but The Terror just came onto my radar when I realized that AMC was turning it into a television show. <b>I'm a book-over-movie/tv adaptation purist.</b> So many details end up falling to the wayside in an adaptation - for example, I've watched one episode of the show, and already spotted a major difference from the book. I knew I'd want to experience this story as Dan Simmons originally told it, so I ran out and got myself a copy. <br><br>I knew going in that this would be a book that would challenge me on a number of fronts. I enjoy horror, but historical fiction is not exactly my purview so to a mix of both is definitely something I'd not experienced before. I'm happy to report that this book far and away exceeded my expectations. <b>This book is as dark and desolate as its setting, packed with perfect atmospheric horror at its greatest.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523040446ra/25335891.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Inspired by real events, <i>The Terror</i> is a fictionalized account of Sir John Franklin's lost expedition of the HMS Erebus and HMS Terror into the artic seas in 1845-1848, to force the Northwest Passage. <b>Dan Simmons weaves together a fictionalized possible explanation to what happened to the men aboard both these sister ships,</b> incorporating both real and supernatural horrors that fill the story with a limitless supply of dread.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523040446ra/25335892.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Some of the best horror is borne out of that same sense of isolation that proliferates this novel. <b>Trapped on the artic ice, in sub-zero temperatures, with a murderous beast hot on their trail,</b> the men of HMS Erebus and HMS Terror already had enough on their plate for me to feel disturbed by. Couple all that with failing food supplies and the gloomy prospect of what must come next when the food runs out, things get even scarier.<br><br>I spent pretty much the entire second half of the story aghast at the levels certain characters are forced to sink to. <b>Make no mistake about it, when people say this book is dark, it is seriously dark.</b> Just when you think things cannot get worse for these characters, they do. Horror fans in general are curtained to be delighted by it, so if you enjoy bleak and existential dread in your horror, you must give this a try. <br><br>One other aspect I really enjoyed about this was the characters. I went into this novel hoping to be impressed by the supernatural bear-demon hunting a trapped crew in the artic and came away feeling like the depth and actions of certain characters really blew that out of the water. <b>I was more compelled by a desire to see how certain characters stories would turn out than I was in the supernatural elements by the end of the novel.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523040446ra/25335893.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Keep in mind that there are a lot of characters here. You've got a cast of 100+ characters counting all the men on both ships, and though many cycle to the forefront of the story only to be excised by death, a few frontrunners who stick around for the long count ended up really capturing my heart. <b>Crozier, Irving, Peglar and Bridgens in particular were three side characters that are so well developed and written that I found myself the most greatly invested in their outcomes.</b><br><br>The level of detail and attention paid to historical accuracy is staggering, though perhaps a little overwhelming to readers who aren't expecting it. I was never bored for a moment and was very pleasantly surprised to encounter a properly scary and well written adventure encapsulated in this horror novel.<br><br><b>4.5 out of 5 stars, rounded up for Goodreads!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1523204735i/25344977._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><i>follow me on instagram</i> <a href="https://www.instagram.com/bookbastion/" rel="nofollow noopener">@bookbastion</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7057344272615893587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_571312801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/571312801" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/571312801?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571312801" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8695435833079657090">Dan Simmons is an author's author. <br/><br/>Every time I read something by him that is either A: not quite in my interest zone, or B: reads workmanlike but nothing particularly brilliant, he SQUASHES my expectations.<br/><br/>HMS Terror and Erebus are out to find the Northwest Passage. In the meantime, I am tricked into caring about every one of the men on the ships. This is not a Darwin Award I'm reading, even though a few characters WERE on the Beagle.<br/><br/>This is a harrowing and perfectly period descent into an icy </span>
  <span id="freeText8695435833079657090" style="display:none">Dan Simmons is an author's author. <br /><br />Every time I read something by him that is either A: not quite in my interest zone, or B: reads workmanlike but nothing particularly brilliant, he SQUASHES my expectations.<br /><br />HMS Terror and Erebus are out to find the Northwest Passage. In the meantime, I am tricked into caring about every one of the men on the ships. This is not a Darwin Award I'm reading, even though a few characters WERE on the Beagle.<br /><br />This is a harrowing and perfectly period descent into an icy hell. Enjoy murder, scurvy, madness, a monster on the ice, wicked dreams, withdrawal, and... of course... SOYLENT GREEN.<br /><br />Oh, wait, wrong book.<br /><br />I'll leave it for posterity. :)<br /><br />At least I never ate human flesh. At least I never ate human flesh. <br /><br />Just keep telling yourself that, buddy.<br /><br />I was lukewarm going into this, but it turned out to be one hell of a brilliant frozen horror. :)<br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText10243470735770358940" style="display:none">Wow... <br /><br />I absolutely loved this book. <br /><br />Don't let the page length stop you from reading it! <span id="freeTextContainer6518568499243648098">Without getting into any spoilers: this is a fictionalized account of the doomed Franklin expedition to find the Northwest Passage in 1845. It is about hubris, greed, strength during unspeakable adversity, and possibly redemption.<br/><br/>Oh, there's also a terrifying monster that they call The Thing on The Ice which is slowly killing everyone aboard the two ships.<br/><br/>It's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons' title='Dan Simmons' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dan Simmons</a>, so he takes his time getting into the meat of the story (my dad said that he was telling three stories when he could have to</span>
  <span id="freeText6518568499243648098" style="display:none">Without getting into any spoilers: this is a fictionalized account of the doomed Franklin expedition to find the Northwest Passage in 1845. It is about hubris, greed, strength during unspeakable adversity, and possibly redemption.<br /><br />Oh, there's also a terrifying monster that they call The Thing on The Ice which is slowly killing everyone aboard the two ships.<br /><br />It's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons" title="Dan Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">Dan Simmons</a>, so he takes his time getting into the meat of the story (my dad said that he was telling three stories when he could have told one) but I consider that to be a feature of his writing, rather than a bug.<br /><br />I absolutely loved this novel. In fact, I loved it so much, I read most of it during JoCoCruiseCrazy in the beginning of 2011, because I just couldn't put it down, even though I was in the middle of the Caribbean on an amazing cruise.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11243327004852403032">WOW! This historic tale of a doomed arctic expedition set in 1845 aboard the HMS TERROR is based on true events and one horrific adventure complete with unbelievably brutal sub-zero temperatures, and a terrifying <i>monster from hell.</i> Loaded with great characters including the mysterious 'Lady Silence' and a unique and surprising ending to say the least. While sometimes descriptively gruesome, an engaging story and thrilling read!</span>

<div id="review_1752315725" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1752315725" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1752315725?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316017459" href="/book/show/2346615.The_Terror">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1752315725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9451505788557629887">“We are all eaters of souls.”<br/><br/>You know those books that you absolutely love, yet wouldn’t blindly recommend them to everyone? That’s me with The Terror. Absolutely LOVED it, but I don’t think it’s suited to every reader.<br/><br/>Incase you didn’t know, The Terror is based on the Franklin Expedition, when two steam-powered vessels set out in 1845 on a mission to traverse the Northwest Passage. So think big ships and lots of snow and ice. But of course, Simmons puts his own spin on it and also throws in ano</span>
  <span id="freeText9451505788557629887" style="display:none">“We are all eaters of souls.”<br /><br />You know those books that you absolutely love, yet wouldn’t blindly recommend them to everyone? That’s me with The Terror. Absolutely LOVED it, but I don’t think it’s suited to every reader.<br /><br />Incase you didn’t know, The Terror is based on the Franklin Expedition, when two steam-powered vessels set out in 1845 on a mission to traverse the Northwest Passage. So think big ships and lots of snow and ice. But of course, Simmons puts his own spin on it and also throws in another threat that is hunting and killing the men. As if the threat of scurvy and hunger isn’t enough!<br /><br />It is clear from the outset that this book is impeccably researched and so it became a learning experience for me as well as being a damn good story! However this is also where I would warn to proceed with caution, as not everyone will enjoy the extreme level of detail given. Some parts of the story are so bloody engrossing and you simply cannot stop turning the pages, but equally you get the lulls where there’s a lot of discussion over how the mission should proceed and so forth. But hey, I loved it all!<br /><br />I truly felt like I embarked on a journey with these men and, boy, was it an emotionally exhausting one. The cast of characters is huge, but you quickly learn who to cheer on, and those you should wish a painful death for. It was horrifying, exhilarating and gut-wrenching. All of the adjectives!!<br /><br />My one minor qualm is the ending - I obviously won’t give away much, but the last 70 pages were so beyond what I was expecting. But this book is all about the journey, so it really didn’t hamper my experience that much! Oh, and some of the detailed descriptions of pubic hair was just... ick.<br /><br />However, I LOOOOOOOVED this! But again, it’s not gonna be for everyone! 4.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9451505788557629887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
